To implement the requested Python program for real-time object detection and tracking on an NVIDIA Jetson Orin NX, we will structure the application into several components. Here's a breakdown of the core classes and functions:

1. **Main Application (main.py)**:
   - **`main()`**: Entry point of the application. Initializes the GUI and starts the detection and tracking process.
   - **`initialize_camera()`**: Sets up the camera feed.
   - **`initialize_yolo()`**: Loads the YOLOv8 model for object detection.
   - **`initialize_tracker()`**: Sets up the DeepSORT or ByteTrack tracker.
   - **`process_frame()`**: Processes each frame for detection and tracking.
   - **`update_gui()`**: Updates the GUI with the latest frame and metadata.

2. **GUI Module (gui.py)**:
   - **`App`**: Class to create and manage the GUI.
   - **`setup_ui()`**: Sets up the user interface components.
   - **`display_frame()`**: Displays the current frame in the GUI.
   - **`display_metadata()`**: Shows real-time metadata.

3. **Detection Module (detection.py)**:
   - **`YOLOv8Detector`**: Class to handle object detection using YOLOv8.
   - **`detect_objects()`**: Method to perform detection on a given frame.

4. **Tracking Module (tracking.py)**:
   - **`Tracker`**: Class to manage object tracking using DeepSORT or ByteTrack.
   - **`update_tracks()`**: Updates the tracker with new detections.

5. **Utilities Module (utils.py)**:
   - **`optimize_with_tensorrt()`**: Function to optimize models with TensorRT for efficiency.

Let's start with the implementation of each file:

### main.py

```python
'''

Main application file for real-time object detection and tracking.

'''

import cv2
from gui import App
from detection import YOLOv8Detector
from tracking import Tracker
from utils import optimize_with_tensorrt

def initialize_camera():
    # Initialize camera feed
    cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)  # Assuming the first camera device
    return cap

def initialize_yolo():
    # Load YOLOv8 model
    detector = YOLOv8Detector()
    return detector

def initialize_tracker():
    # Initialize tracker
    tracker = Tracker()
    return tracker

def process_frame(frame, detector, tracker):
    # Detect objects
    detections = detector.detect_objects(frame)
    # Update tracker
    tracks = tracker.update_tracks(detections)
    return tracks

def main():
    # Initialize components
    cap = initialize_camera()
    detector = initialize_yolo()
    tracker = initialize_tracker()

    # Optimize models with TensorRT
    optimize_with_tensorrt(detector)

    # Initialize GUI
    app = App()

    while True:
        ret, frame = cap.read()
        if not ret:
            break

        # Process frame
        tracks = process_frame(frame, detector, tracker)

        # Update GUI
        app.display_frame(frame)
        app.display_metadata(tracks)

        # Break on 'q' key press
        if cv2.waitKey(1) & 0xFF == ord('q'):
            break

    cap.release()
    cv2.destroyAllWindows()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

### gui.py

```python
'''

GUI module for displaying video feed and metadata.

'''

import cv2
from tkinter import Tk, Label

class App:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = Tk()
        self.setup_ui()

    def setup_ui(self):
        self.root.title("Object Detection and Tracking")
        self.label = Label(self.root)
        self.label.pack()

    def display_frame(self, frame):
        # Convert frame to a format suitable for Tkinter
        cv2.imshow("Frame", frame)

    def display_metadata(self, tracks):
        # Display metadata in the GUI
        print("Tracks:", tracks)

    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()
```

```python
'''

Main application file for real-time object detection and tracking.

'''

import cv2
from gui import App
from detection import YOLOv8Detector
from tracking import Tracker
from utils import optimize_with_tensorrt

def initialize_camera():
    # Initialize camera feed
    cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)  # Assuming the first camera device
    return cap

def initialize_yolo():
    # Load YOLOv8 model
    detector = YOLOv8Detector()
    return detector

def initialize_tracker():
    # Initialize tracker
    tracker = Tracker()
    return tracker

def process_frame(frame, detector, tracker):
    # Detect objects
    detections = detector.detect_objects(frame)
    # Update tracker
    tracks = tracker.update_tracks(detections)
    return tracks

def main():
    # Initialize components
    cap = initialize_camera()
    detector = initialize_yolo()
    tracker = initialize_tracker()

    # Optimize models with TensorRT
    optimize_with_tensorrt(detector)

    # Initialize GUI
    app = App()

    while True:
        ret, frame = cap.read()
        if not ret:
            break

        # Process frame
        tracks = process_frame(frame, detector, tracker)

        # Update GUI
        app.display_frame(frame)
        app.display_metadata(tracks)

        # Break on 'q' key press
        if cv2.waitKey(1) & 0xFF == ord('q'):
            break

    cap.release()
    cv2.destroyAllWindows()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

```python
'''
Main application file for real-time object detection and tracking.
'''
import cv2
from gui import App
from detection import YOLOv8Detector
from tracking import Tracker
from utils import optimize_with_tensorrt
def initialize_camera():
    # Initialize camera feed
    cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)  # Assuming the first camera device
    return cap
def initialize_yolo():
    # Load YOLOv8 model
    detector = YOLOv8Detector()
    return detector
def initialize_tracker():
    # Initialize tracker
    tracker = Tracker()
    return tracker
def process_frame(frame, detector, tracker):
    # Detect objects
    detections = detector.detect_objects(frame)
    # Update tracker
    tracks = tracker.update_tracks(detections)
    return tracks
def main():
    # Initialize components
    cap = initialize_camera()
    detector = initialize_yolo()
    tracker = initialize_tracker()
    # Optimize models with TensorRT
    optimize_with_tensorrt(detector)
    # Initialize GUI
    app = App()
    while True:
        ret, frame = cap.read()
        if not ret:
            break
        # Process frame
        tracks = process_frame(frame, detector, tracker)
        # Update GUI
        app.display_frame(frame)
        app.display_metadata(tracks)
        # Break on 'q' key press
        if cv2.waitKey(1) & 0xFF == ord('q'):
            break
    cap.release()
    cv2.destroyAllWindows()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

### detection.py
```python
'''
Detection module using YOLOv8.
'''
import torch
from ultralytics import YOLO

class YOLOv8Detector:
    def __init__(self, model_path='yolov8.pt'):
        # Load YOLOv8 model
        self.model = YOLO(model_path)
    
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Perform object detection
        results = self.model(frame)
        detections = []
        for result in results.xyxy[0]:  # Assuming results are in xyxy format
            x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = result
            detections.append({
                'bbox': [x1.item(), y1.item(), x2.item(), y2.item()],
                'confidence': conf.item(),
                'class': int(cls.item())
            })
        return detections
```

### main.py
```python
'''
Main application file for real-time object detection and tracking.
'''
import cv2
from gui import App
from detection import YOLOv8Detector
from tracking import Tracker
from utils import optimize_with_tensorrt

def initialize_camera():
    # Initialize camera feed
    cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)  # Assuming the first camera device
    return cap

def initialize_yolo():
    # Load YOLOv8 model
    detector = YOLOv8Detector()
    return detector

def initialize_tracker():
    # Initialize tracker
    tracker = Tracker()
    return tracker

def process_frame(frame, detector, tracker):
    # Detect objects
    detections = detector.detect_objects(frame)
    # Update tracker
    tracks = tracker.update_tracks(detections)
    return tracks

def main():
    # Initialize components
    cap = initialize_camera()
    detector = initialize_yolo()
    tracker = initialize_tracker()
    # Optimize models with TensorRT
    optimize_with_tensorrt(detector)
    # Initialize GUI
    app = App()
    while True:
        ret, frame = cap.read()
        if not ret:
            break
        # Process frame
        tracks = process_frame(frame, detector, tracker)
        # Update GUI
        app.display_frame(frame)
        app.display_metadata(tracks)
        # Break on 'q' key press
        if cv2.waitKey(1) & 0xFF == ord('q'):
            break
    cap.release()
    cv2.destroyAllWindows()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

```python
'''
Detection module using YOLOv8.
'''
import torch
from ultralytics import YOLO

class YOLOv8Detector:
    def __init__(self, model_path='yolov8.pt'):
        # Load YOLOv8 model
        self.model = YOLO(model_path)
    
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        # Perform object detection
        results = self.model(frame)
        detections = []
        for result in results.xyxy[0]:  # Assuming results are in xyxy format
            x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = result
            detections.append({
                'bbox': [x1.item(), y1.item(), x2.item(), y2.item()],
                'confidence': conf.item(),
                'class': int(cls.item())
            })
        return detections
```

### main.py
```python
'''
Main application file for real-time object detection and tracking.
'''
import cv2
from gui import App
from detection import YOLOv8Detector
from tracking import Tracker
from utils import optimize_with_tensorrt

def initialize_camera():
    # Initialize camera feed
    cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)  # Assuming the first camera device
    return cap

def initialize_yolo():
    # Load YOLOv8 model
    detector = YOLOv8Detector()
    return detector

def initialize_tracker():
    # Initialize tracker
    tracker = Tracker()
    return tracker

def process_frame(frame, detector, tracker):
    # Detect objects
    detections = detector.detect_objects(frame)
    # Update tracker
    tracks = tracker.update_tracks(detections)
    return tracks

def main():
    # Initialize components
    cap = initialize_camera()
    detector = initialize_yolo()
    tracker = initialize_tracker()
    # Optimize models with TensorRT
    optimize_with_tensorrt(detector)
    # Initialize GUI
    app = App()
    while True:
        ret, frame = cap.read()
        if not ret:
            break
        # Process frame
        tracks = process_frame(frame, detector, tracker)
        # Update GUI
        app.display_frame(frame)
        app.display_metadata(tracks)
        # Break on 'q' key press
        if cv2.waitKey(1) & 0xFF == ord('q'):
            break
    cap.release()
    cv2.destroyAllWindows()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

To implement the `utils.py` file and ensure the complete functionality of the software, we need to implement the `optimize_with_tensorrt` function. This function will optimize the YOLOv8 model using TensorRT for better performance on the NVIDIA Jetson Orin NX. Below is the fully implemented code for `utils.py` and any necessary adjustments to other files:

### utils.py
```python
'''
Utility functions for optimization and other tasks.
'''
import tensorrt as trt
import pycuda.driver as cuda
import pycuda.autoinit

def optimize_with_tensorrt(detector):
    '''
    Optimize the YOLOv8 model with TensorRT.
    '''
    # Create a TensorRT logger
    logger = trt.Logger(trt.Logger.WARNING)
    
    # Create a builder and network
    builder = trt.Builder(logger)
    network = builder.create_network(1 << int(trt.NetworkDefinitionCreationFlag.EXPLICIT_BATCH))
    
    # Parse the ONNX model to TensorRT
    onnx_path = 'yolov8.onnx'  # Assuming the model is converted to ONNX format
    with trt.OnnxParser(network, logger) as parser:
        with open(onnx_path, 'rb') as model:
            if not parser.parse(model.read()):
                print('ERROR: Failed to parse the ONNX file.')
                for error in range(parser.num_errors):
                    print(parser.get_error(error))
                return
    
    # Build the engine
    builder.max_workspace_size = 1 << 30  # 1GB
    builder.max_batch_size = 1
    engine = builder.build_cuda_engine(network)
    
    # Allocate buffers for input and output
    input_shape = network.get_input(0).shape
    output_shape = network.get_output(0).shape
    input_size = trt.volume(input_shape) * trt.float32.itemsize
    output_size = trt.volume(output_shape) * trt.float32.itemsize
    
    d_input = cuda.mem_alloc(input_size)
    d_output = cuda.mem_alloc(output_size)
    
    # Create a context
    context = engine.create_execution_context()
    
    # Store the optimized engine and context in the detector
    detector.engine = engine
    detector.context = context
    detector.d_input = d_input
    detector.d_output = d_output
    detector.input_shape = input_shape
    detector.output_shape = output_shape
```

### detection.py (adjustments)
```python
'''
Detection module using YOLOv8.
'''
import torch
from ultralytics import YOLO
import numpy as np
import pycuda.driver as cuda

class YOLOv8Detector:
    def __init__(self, model_path='yolov8.pt'):
        # Load YOLOv8 model
        self.model = YOLO(model_path)
        self.engine = None
        self.context = None
        self.d_input = None
        self.d_output = None
        self.input_shape = None
        self.output_shape = None

    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        if self.engine is not None:
            # Preprocess the frame
            frame_resized = cv2.resize(frame, (self.input_shape[2], self.input_shape[1]))
            frame_normalized = frame_resized.astype(np.float32) / 255.0
            frame_transposed = np.transpose(frame_normalized, (2, 0, 1)).ravel()
            
            # Transfer input data to the GPU
            cuda.memcpy_htod(self.d_input, frame_transposed)
            
            # Run inference
            self.context.execute_v2(bindings=[int(self.d_input), int(self.d_output)])
            
            # Transfer predictions back from the GPU
            output = np.empty(self.output_shape, dtype=np.float32)
            cuda.memcpy_dtoh(output, self.d_output)
            
            # Process output
            detections = self.process_output(output)
        else:
            # Fallback to PyTorch model if TensorRT is not available
            results = self.model(frame)
            detections = []
            for result in results.xyxy[0]:  # Assuming results are in xyxy format
                x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = result
                detections.append({
                    'bbox': [x1.item(), y1.item(), x2.item(), y2.item()],
                    'confidence': conf.item(),
                    'class': int(cls.item())
                })
        return detections

    def process_output(self, output):
        # Process the output from TensorRT inference
        detections = []
        for det in output:
            x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = det
            detections.append({
                'bbox': [x1, y1, x2, y2],
                'confidence': conf,
                'class': int(cls)
            })
        return detections
```

This implementation assumes that the YOLOv8 model has been converted to ONNX format, which is necessary for TensorRT optimization. The `optimize_with_tensorrt` function sets up the TensorRT engine and context, and the `YOLOv8Detector` class has been modified to use this optimized engine for inference when available.

### utils.py
```python
'''
Utility functions for optimization and other tasks.
'''
import tensorrt as trt
import pycuda.driver as cuda
import pycuda.autoinit

def optimize_with_tensorrt(detector):
    '''
    Optimize the YOLOv8 model with TensorRT.
    '''
    # Create a TensorRT logger
    logger = trt.Logger(trt.Logger.WARNING)
    
    # Create a builder and network
    builder = trt.Builder(logger)
    network = builder.create_network(1 << int(trt.NetworkDefinitionCreationFlag.EXPLICIT_BATCH))
    
    # Parse the ONNX model to TensorRT
    onnx_path = 'yolov8.onnx'  # Assuming the model is converted to ONNX format
    with trt.OnnxParser(network, logger) as parser:
        with open(onnx_path, 'rb') as model:
            if not parser.parse(model.read()):
                print('ERROR: Failed to parse the ONNX file.')
                for error in range(parser.num_errors):
                    print(parser.get_error(error))
                return
    
    # Build the engine
    builder.max_workspace_size = 1 << 30  # 1GB
    builder.max_batch_size = 1
    engine = builder.build_cuda_engine(network)
    
    # Allocate buffers for input and output
    input_shape = network.get_input(0).shape
    output_shape = network.get_output(0).shape
    input_size = trt.volume(input_shape) * trt.float32.itemsize
    output_size = trt.volume(output_shape) * trt.float32.itemsize
    
    d_input = cuda.mem_alloc(input_size)
    d_output = cuda.mem_alloc(output_size)
    
    # Create a context
    context = engine.create_execution_context()
    
    # Store the optimized engine and context in the detector
    detector.engine = engine
    detector.context = context
    detector.d_input = d_input
    detector.d_output = d_output
    detector.input_shape = input_shape
    detector.output_shape = output_shape
```

### detection.py (adjustments)
```python
'''
Detection module using YOLOv8.
'''
import torch
from ultralytics import YOLO
import numpy as np
import pycuda.driver as cuda

class YOLOv8Detector:
    def __init__(self, model_path='yolov8.pt'):
        # Load YOLOv8 model
        self.model = YOLO(model_path)
        self.engine = None
        self.context = None
        self.d_input = None
        self.d_output = None
        self.input_shape = None
        self.output_shape = None

    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        if self.engine is not None:
            # Preprocess the frame
            frame_resized = cv2.resize(frame, (self.input_shape[2], self.input_shape[1]))
            frame_normalized = frame_resized.astype(np.float32) / 255.0
            frame_transposed = np.transpose(frame_normalized, (2, 0, 1)).ravel()
            
            # Transfer input data to the GPU
            cuda.memcpy_htod(self.d_input, frame_transposed)
            
            # Run inference
            self.context.execute_v2(bindings=[int(self.d_input), int(self.d_output)])
            
            # Transfer predictions back from the GPU
            output = np.empty(self.output_shape, dtype=np.float32)
            cuda.memcpy_dtoh(output, self.d_output)
            
            # Process output
            detections = self.process_output(output)
        else:
            # Fallback to PyTorch model if TensorRT is not available
            results = self.model(frame)
            detections = []
            for result in results.xyxy[0]:  # Assuming results are in xyxy format
                x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = result
                detections.append({
                    'bbox': [x1.item(), y1.item(), x2.item(), y2.item()],
                    'confidence': conf.item(),
                    'class': int(cls.item())
                })
        return detections

    def process_output(self, output):
        # Process the output from TensorRT inference
        detections = []
        for det in output:
            x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = det
            detections.append({
                'bbox': [x1, y1, x2, y2],
                'confidence': conf,
                'class': int(cls)
            })
        return detections
```

This implementation assumes that the YOLOv8 model has been converted to ONNX format, which is necessary for TensorRT optimization. The `optimize_with_tensorrt` function sets up the TensorRT engine and context, and the `YOLOv8Detector` class has been modified to use this optimized engine for inference when available.

"main.py
```python
'''
Main application file for real-time object detection and tracking.
'''
import cv2
from gui import App
from detection import YOLOv8Detector
from tracking import Tracker
from utils import optimize_with_tensorrt
def initialize_camera():
    # Initialize camera feed
    cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)  # Assuming the first camera device
    return cap
def initialize_yolo():
    # Load YOLOv8 model
    detector = YOLOv8Detector()
    return detector
def initialize_tracker():
    # Initialize tracker
    tracker = Tracker()
    return tracker
def process_frame(frame, detector, tracker):
    # Detect objects
    detections = detector.detect_objects(frame)
    # Update tracker
    tracks = tracker.update_tracks(detections)
    return tracks
def main():
    # Initialize components
    cap = initialize_camera()
    detector = initialize_yolo()
    tracker = initialize_tracker()
    # Optimize models with TensorRT
    optimize_with_tensorrt(detector)
    # Initialize GUI
    app = App()
    while True:
        ret, frame = cap.read()
        if not ret:
            break
        # Process frame
        tracks = process_frame(frame, detector, tracker)
        # Update GUI
        app.display_frame(frame)
        app.display_metadata(tracks)
        # Break on 'q' key press
        if cv2.waitKey(1) & 0xFF == ord('q'):
            break
    cap.release()
    cv2.destroyAllWindows()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

```python
'''
GUI module for displaying video feed and metadata.
'''
import cv2
from tkinter import Tk, Label
class App:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = Tk()
        self.setup_ui()
    def setup_ui(self):
        self.root.title("Object Detection and Tracking")
        self.label = Label(self.root)
        self.label.pack()
    def display_frame(self, frame):
        # Convert frame to a format suitable for Tkinter
        cv2.imshow("Frame", frame)
    def display_metadata(self, tracks):
        # Display metadata in the GUI
        print("Tracks:", tracks)
    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()
```

detection.py
```python
'''
Detection module using YOLOv8.
'''
import torch
from ultralytics import YOLO
import numpy as np
import pycuda.driver as cuda
class YOLOv8Detector:
    def __init__(self, model_path='yolov8.pt'):
        # Load YOLOv8 model
        self.model = YOLO(model_path)
        self.engine = None
        self.context = None
        self.d_input = None
        self.d_output = None
        self.input_shape = None
        self.output_shape = None
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        if self.engine is not None:
            # Preprocess the frame
            frame_resized = cv2.resize(frame, (self.input_shape[2], self.input_shape[1]))
            frame_normalized = frame_resized.astype(np.float32) / 255.0
            frame_transposed = np.transpose(frame_normalized, (2, 0, 1)).ravel()
            # Transfer input data to the GPU
            cuda.memcpy_htod(self.d_input, frame_transposed)
            # Run inference
            self.context.execute_v2(bindings=[int(self.d_input), int(self.d_output)])
            # Transfer predictions back from the GPU
            output = np.empty(self.output_shape, dtype=np.float32)
            cuda.memcpy_dtoh(output, self.d_output)
            # Process output
            detections = self.process_output(output)
        else:
            # Fallback to PyTorch model if TensorRT is not available
            results = self.model(frame)
            detections = []
            for result in results.xyxy[0]:  # Assuming results are in xyxy format
                x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = result
                detections.append({
                    'bbox': [x1.item(), y1.item(), x2.item(), y2.item()],
                    'confidence': conf.item(),
                    'class': int(cls.item())
                })
        return detections
    def process_output(self, output):
        # Process the output from TensorRT inference
        detections = []
        for det in output:
            x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = det
            detections.append({
                'bbox': [x1, y1, x2, y2],
                'confidence': conf,
                'class': int(cls)
            })
        return detections
```

utils.py
```python
'''
Utility functions for optimization and other tasks.
'''
import tensorrt as trt
import pycuda.driver as cuda
import pycuda.autoinit
def optimize_with_tensorrt(detector):
    '''
    Optimize the YOLOv8 model with TensorRT.
    '''
    # Create a TensorRT logger
    logger = trt.Logger(trt.Logger.WARNING)
    # Create a builder and network
    builder = trt.Builder(logger)
    network = builder.create_network(1 << int(trt.NetworkDefinitionCreationFlag.EXPLICIT_BATCH))
    # Parse the ONNX model to TensorRT
    onnx_path = 'yolov8.onnx'  # Assuming the model is converted to ONNX format
    with trt.OnnxParser(network, logger) as parser:
        with open(onnx_path, 'rb') as model:
            if not parser.parse(model.read()):
                print('ERROR: Failed to parse the ONNX file.')
                for error in range(parser.num_errors):
                    print(parser.get_error(error))
                return
    # Build the engine
    builder.max_workspace_size = 1 << 30  # 1GB
    builder.max_batch_size = 1
    engine = builder.build_cuda_engine(network)
    # Allocate buffers for input and output
    input_shape = network.get_input(0).shape
    output_shape = network.get_output(0).shape
    input_size = trt.volume(input_shape) * trt.float32.itemsize
    output_size = trt.volume(output_shape) * trt.float32.itemsize
    d_input = cuda.mem_alloc(input_size)
    d_output = cuda.mem_alloc(output_size)
    # Create a context
    context = engine.create_execution_context()
    # Store the optimized engine and context in the detector
    detector.engine = engine
    detector.context = context
    detector.d_input = d_input
    detector.d_output = d_output
    detector.input_shape = input_shape
    detector.output_shape = output_shape
```

Certainly! To complete the implementation of the `tracking.py` file, we will use DeepSORT for tracking. Below is the fully implemented code for the `tracking.py` file, along with the necessary modifications to other files to ensure the program functions correctly. 

**tracking.py**
```python
'''
Tracking module using DeepSORT.
'''
from deep_sort.deep_sort import DeepSort
import numpy as np

class Tracker:
    def __init__(self):
        # Initialize DeepSORT tracker
        self.tracker = DeepSort(
            model_path='deep_sort_model.ckpt',  # Path to the DeepSORT model
            max_dist=0.2,
            min_confidence=0.3,
            nms_max_overlap=0.5,
            max_iou_distance=0.7,
            max_age=70,
            n_init=3,
            nn_budget=100
        )

    def update_tracks(self, detections):
        # Convert detections to the format required by DeepSORT
        bbox_xywh = np.array([det['bbox'] for det in detections])
        confidences = np.array([det['confidence'] for det in detections])
        classes = np.array([det['class'] for det in detections])

        # Update tracker with new detections
        tracks = self.tracker.update(bbox_xywh, confidences, classes)

        # Format tracks for output
        formatted_tracks = []
        for track in tracks:
            formatted_tracks.append({
                'track_id': track.track_id,
                'bbox': track.to_tlbr(),
                'class': track.cls,
                'confidence': track.confidence
            })

        return formatted_tracks
```

```python
'''

from gui import App
from detection import YOLOv8Detector
from tracking import Tracker
from utils import optimize_with_tensorrt

def initialize_camera():
    # Initialize camera feed

    return cap

    # Load YOLOv8 model
    detector = YOLOv8Detector()
    return detector

def initialize_tracker():
    # Initialize tracker
    tracker = Tracker()
    return tracker

def process_frame(frame, detector, tracker):
    # Detect objects
    detections = detector.detect_objects(frame)
    # Update tracker
    tracks = tracker.update_tracks(detections)
    return tracks

def main():
    # Initialize components
    cap = initialize_camera()
    detector = initialize_yolo()
    tracker = initialize_tracker()
    # Optimize models with TensorRT
    optimize_with_tensorrt(detector)
    # Initialize GUI
    app = App()
    while True:
        ret, frame = cap.read()
        if not ret:
            break
        # Process frame
        tracks = process_frame(frame, detector, tracker)
        # Update GUI

        app.display_metadata(tracks)

    cv2.destroyAllWindows()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

```python
Detection module using YOLOv8.
'''
import torch
from ultralytics import YOLO
import numpy as np
import pycuda.driver as cuda

class YOLOv8Detector:
    def __init__(self, model_path='yolov8.pt'):
        # Load YOLOv8 model
        self.model = YOLO(model_path)
        self.engine = None
        self.context = None
        self.d_input = None
        self.d_output = None
        self.input_shape = None
        self.output_shape = None

    def detect_objects(self, frame):

            frame_normalized = frame_resized.astype(np.float32) / 255.0
            frame_transposed = np.transpose(frame_normalized, (2, 0, 1)).ravel()
            # Transfer input data to the GPU
            cuda.memcpy_htod(self.d_input, frame_transposed)
            # Run inference
            self.context.execute_v2(bindings=[int(self.d_input), int(self.d_output)])
            # Transfer predictions back from the GPU
            output = np.empty(self.output_shape, dtype=np.float32)
            cuda.memcpy_dtoh(output, self.d_output)
            # Process output
            detections = self.process_output(output)
        else:
            # Fallback to PyTorch model if TensorRT is not available
            results = self.model(frame)
            detections = []
            for result in results.xyxy[0]:  # Assuming results are in xyxy format
                x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = result
                detections.append({
                    'bbox': [x1.item(), y1.item(), x2.item(), y2.item()],
                    'confidence': conf.item(),
                    'class': int(cls.item())
                })
        return detections

    def process_output(self, output):
        # Process the output from TensorRT inference
        detections = []
        for det in output:
            x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = det
            detections.append({
                'bbox': [x1, y1, x2, y2],
                'confidence': conf,
                'class': int(cls)
            })
        return detections
```

```python
'''
Utility functions for optimization and other tasks.
'''
import tensorrt as trt
import pycuda.driver as cuda
import pycuda.autoinit

def optimize_with_tensorrt(detector):
    '''
    Optimize the YOLOv8 model with TensorRT.
    '''
    # Create a TensorRT logger
    logger = trt.Logger(trt.Logger.WARNING)
    # Create a builder and network
    builder = trt.Builder(logger)
    network = builder.create_network(1 << int(trt.NetworkDefinitionCreationFlag.EXPLICIT_BATCH))
    # Parse the ONNX model to TensorRT
    onnx_path = 'yolov8.onnx'  # Assuming the model is converted to ONNX format
    with trt.OnnxParser(network, logger) as parser:
        with open(onnx_path, 'rb') as model:
            if not parser.parse(model.read()):
                print('ERROR: Failed to parse the ONNX file.')
                for error in range(parser.num_errors):
                    print(parser.get_error(error))
                return
    # Build the engine
    builder.max_workspace_size = 1 << 30  # 1GB
    builder.max_batch_size = 1
    engine = builder.build_cuda_engine(network)
    # Allocate buffers for input and output
    input_shape = network.get_input(0).shape
    output_shape = network.get_output(0).shape
    input_size = trt.volume(input_shape) * trt.float32.itemsize
    output_size = trt.volume(output_shape) * trt.float32.itemsize
    d_input = cuda.mem_alloc(input_size)
    d_output = cuda.mem_alloc(output_size)
    # Create a context
    context = engine.create_execution_context()
    # Store the optimized engine and context in the detector
    detector.engine = engine
    detector.context = context
    detector.d_input = d_input
    detector.d_output = d_output
    detector.input_shape = input_shape
    detector.output_shape = output_shape
```

```python
class Tracker:
    def __init__(self):
        # Initialize DeepSORT tracker
        self.tracker = DeepSort(
            model_path='deep_sort_model.ckpt',  # Path to the DeepSORT model
            max_dist=0.2,
            min_confidence=0.3,
            nms_max_overlap=0.5,
            max_iou_distance=0.7,
            max_age=70,
            n_init=3,
            nn_budget=100
        )

    def update_tracks(self, detections):

        bbox_xywh = np.array([det['bbox'] for det in detections])
        confidences = np.array([det['confidence'] for det in detections])
        classes = np.array([det['class'] for det in detections])

        # Update tracker with new detections

                'class': track.cls,
                'confidence': track.confidence

        return formatted_tracks
```

```python
'''
Detection module using YOLOv8.
'''
import torch
from ultralytics import YOLO
import numpy as np
import pycuda.driver as cuda

class YOLOv8Detector:
    def __init__(self, model_path='yolov8.pt'):
        # Load YOLOv8 model
        self.model = YOLO(model_path)
        self.engine = None
        self.context = None
        self.d_input = None
        self.d_output = None
        self.input_shape = None
        self.output_shape = None

    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        if self.engine is not None:
            # Preprocess the frame
            frame_resized = cv2.resize(frame, (self.input_shape[2], self.input_shape[1]))
            frame_normalized = frame_resized.astype(np.float32) / 255.0
            frame_transposed = np.transpose(frame_normalized, (2, 0, 1)).ravel()
            # Transfer input data to the GPU
            cuda.memcpy_htod(self.d_input, frame_transposed)
            # Run inference
            self.context.execute_v2(bindings=[int(self.d_input), int(self.d_output)])
            # Transfer predictions back from the GPU
            output = np.empty(self.output_shape, dtype=np.float32)
            cuda.memcpy_dtoh(output, self.d_output)
            # Process output
            detections = self.process_output(output)
        else:
            # Fallback to PyTorch model if TensorRT is not available
            results = self.model(frame)
            detections = []
            for result in results.xyxy[0]:  # Assuming results are in xyxy format
                x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = result
                detections.append({
                    'bbox': [x1.item(), y1.item(), x2.item(), y2.item()],
                    'confidence': conf.item(),
                    'class': int(cls.item())
                })
        return detections

    def process_output(self, output):
        # Process the output from TensorRT inference
        detections = []
        for det in output:
            x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = det
            detections.append({
                'bbox': [x1, y1, x2, y2],
                'confidence': conf,
                'class': int(cls)
            })
        return detections
```

**utils.py**
```python
'''
Utility functions for optimization and other tasks.
'''
import tensorrt as trt
import pycuda.driver as cuda
import pycuda.autoinit

def optimize_with_tensorrt(detector):
    '''
    Optimize the YOLOv8 model with TensorRT.
    '''
    # Create a TensorRT logger
    logger = trt.Logger(trt.Logger.WARNING)
    # Create a builder and network
    builder = trt.Builder(logger)
    network = builder.create_network(1 << int(trt.NetworkDefinitionCreationFlag.EXPLICIT_BATCH))
    # Parse the ONNX model to TensorRT
    onnx_path = 'yolov8.onnx'  # Assuming the model is converted to ONNX format
    with trt.OnnxParser(network, logger) as parser:
        with open(onnx_path, 'rb') as model:
            if not parser.parse(model.read()):
                print('ERROR: Failed to parse the ONNX file.')
                for error in range(parser.num_errors):
                    print(parser.get_error(error))
                return
    # Build the engine
    builder.max_workspace_size = 1 << 30  # 1GB
    builder.max_batch_size = 1
    engine = builder.build_cuda_engine(network)
    # Allocate buffers for input and output
    input_shape = network.get_input(0).shape
    output_shape = network.get_output(0).shape
    input_size = trt.volume(input_shape) * trt.float32.itemsize
    output_size = trt.volume(output_shape) * trt.float32.itemsize
    d_input = cuda.mem_alloc(input_size)
    d_output = cuda.mem_alloc(output_size)
    # Create a context
    context = engine.create_execution_context()
    # Store the optimized engine and context in the detector
    detector.engine = engine
    detector.context = context
    detector.d_input = d_input
    detector.d_output = d_output
    detector.input_shape = input_shape
    detector.output_shape = output_shape
```

This implementation completes the tracking functionality using DeepSORT, integrates it with the detection system, and ensures the program can process real-time video feeds for object detection and tracking.

"main.py
```python
'''
Main application file for real-time object detection and tracking.
'''
import cv2
from gui import App
from detection import YOLOv8Detector
from tracking import Tracker
from utils import optimize_with_tensorrt
def initialize_camera():
    # Initialize camera feed
    cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)  # Assuming the first camera device
    return cap
def initialize_yolo():
    # Load YOLOv8 model
    detector = YOLOv8Detector()
    return detector
def initialize_tracker():
    # Initialize tracker
    tracker = Tracker()
    return tracker
def process_frame(frame, detector, tracker):
    # Detect objects
    detections = detector.detect_objects(frame)
    # Update tracker
    tracks = tracker.update_tracks(detections)
    return tracks
def main():
    # Initialize components
    cap = initialize_camera()
    detector = initialize_yolo()
    tracker = initialize_tracker()
    # Optimize models with TensorRT
    optimize_with_tensorrt(detector)
    # Initialize GUI
    app = App()
    while True:
        ret, frame = cap.read()
        if not ret:
            break
        # Process frame
        tracks = process_frame(frame, detector, tracker)
        # Update GUI
        app.display_frame(frame)
        app.display_metadata(tracks)
        # Break on 'q' key press
        if cv2.waitKey(1) & 0xFF == ord('q'):
            break
    cap.release()
    cv2.destroyAllWindows()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

```python
'''
GUI module for displaying video feed and metadata.
'''
import cv2
from tkinter import Tk, Label
class App:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = Tk()
        self.setup_ui()
    def setup_ui(self):
        self.root.title("Object Detection and Tracking")
        self.label = Label(self.root)
        self.label.pack()
    def display_frame(self, frame):
        # Convert frame to a format suitable for Tkinter
        cv2.imshow("Frame", frame)
    def display_metadata(self, tracks):
        # Display metadata in the GUI
        print("Tracks:", tracks)
    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()
```

detection.py
```python
'''
Detection module using YOLOv8.
'''
import torch
from ultralytics import YOLO
import numpy as np
import pycuda.driver as cuda
class YOLOv8Detector:
    def __init__(self, model_path='yolov8.pt'):
        # Load YOLOv8 model
        self.model = YOLO(model_path)
        self.engine = None
        self.context = None
        self.d_input = None
        self.d_output = None
        self.input_shape = None
        self.output_shape = None
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        if self.engine is not None:
            # Preprocess the frame
            frame_resized = cv2.resize(frame, (self.input_shape[2], self.input_shape[1]))
            frame_normalized = frame_resized.astype(np.float32) / 255.0
            frame_transposed = np.transpose(frame_normalized, (2, 0, 1)).ravel()
            # Transfer input data to the GPU
            cuda.memcpy_htod(self.d_input, frame_transposed)
            # Run inference
            self.context.execute_v2(bindings=[int(self.d_input), int(self.d_output)])
            # Transfer predictions back from the GPU
            output = np.empty(self.output_shape, dtype=np.float32)
            cuda.memcpy_dtoh(output, self.d_output)
            # Process output
            detections = self.process_output(output)
        else:
            # Fallback to PyTorch model if TensorRT is not available
            results = self.model(frame)
            detections = []
            for result in results.xyxy[0]:  # Assuming results are in xyxy format
                x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = result
                detections.append({
                    'bbox': [x1.item(), y1.item(), x2.item(), y2.item()],
                    'confidence': conf.item(),
                    'class': int(cls.item())
                })
        return detections
    def process_output(self, output):
        # Process the output from TensorRT inference
        detections = []
        for det in output:
            x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = det
            detections.append({
                'bbox': [x1, y1, x2, y2],
                'confidence': conf,
                'class': int(cls)
            })
        return detections
```

tracking.py
```python
'''
Tracking module using DeepSORT.
'''
from deep_sort.deep_sort import DeepSort
import numpy as np
class Tracker:
    def __init__(self):
        # Initialize DeepSORT tracker
        self.tracker = DeepSort(
            model_path='deep_sort_model.ckpt',  # Path to the DeepSORT model
            max_dist=0.2,
            min_confidence=0.3,
            nms_max_overlap=0.5,
            max_iou_distance=0.7,
            max_age=70,
            n_init=3,
            nn_budget=100
        )
    def update_tracks(self, detections):
        # Convert detections to the format required by DeepSORT
        bbox_xywh = np.array([det['bbox'] for det in detections])
        confidences = np.array([det['confidence'] for det in detections])
        classes = np.array([det['class'] for det in detections])
        # Update tracker with new detections
        tracks = self.tracker.update(bbox_xywh, confidences, classes)
        # Format tracks for output
        formatted_tracks = []
        for track in tracks:
            formatted_tracks.append({
                'track_id': track.track_id,
                'bbox': track.to_tlbr(),
                'class': track.cls,
                'confidence': track.confidence
            })
        return formatted_tracks
```

utils.py
```python
'''
Utility functions for optimization and other tasks.
'''
import tensorrt as trt
import pycuda.driver as cuda
import pycuda.autoinit
def optimize_with_tensorrt(detector):
    '''
    Optimize the YOLOv8 model with TensorRT.
    '''
    # Create a TensorRT logger
    logger = trt.Logger(trt.Logger.WARNING)
    # Create a builder and network
    builder = trt.Builder(logger)
    network = builder.create_network(1 << int(trt.NetworkDefinitionCreationFlag.EXPLICIT_BATCH))
    # Parse the ONNX model to TensorRT
    onnx_path = 'yolov8.onnx'  # Assuming the model is converted to ONNX format
    with trt.OnnxParser(network, logger) as parser:
        with open(onnx_path, 'rb') as model:
            if not parser.parse(model.read()):
                print('ERROR: Failed to parse the ONNX file.')
                for error in range(parser.num_errors):
                    print(parser.get_error(error))
                return
    # Build the engine
    builder.max_workspace_size = 1 << 30  # 1GB
    builder.max_batch_size = 1
    engine = builder.build_cuda_engine(network)
    # Allocate buffers for input and output
    input_shape = network.get_input(0).shape
    output_shape = network.get_output(0).shape
    input_size = trt.volume(input_shape) * trt.float32.itemsize
    output_size = trt.volume(output_shape) * trt.float32.itemsize
    d_input = cuda.mem_alloc(input_size)
    d_output = cuda.mem_alloc(output_size)
    # Create a context
    context = engine.create_execution_context()
    # Store the optimized engine and context in the detector
    detector.engine = engine
    detector.context = context
    detector.d_input = d_input
    detector.d_output = d_output
    detector.input_shape = input_shape
    detector.output_shape = output_shape
```

To fix this, you should integrate the video feed display into the Tkinter GUI instead of using `cv2.imshow`. Here's a suggestion on how to do it:

1. Convert the OpenCV frame to a format that Tkinter can display (e.g., using PIL or directly with Tkinter's PhotoImage).
2. Update the `display_frame` method in `gui.py` to use Tkinter widgets for displaying the video feed.

Here's an example modification for the `display_frame` method:

```python
from PIL import Image, ImageTk

def display_frame(self, frame):
    # Convert the frame to RGB format
    frame_rgb = cv2.cvtColor(frame, cv2.COLOR_BGR2RGB)
    # Convert the frame to a PIL Image
    image = Image.fromarray(frame_rgb)
    # Convert the PIL Image to a PhotoImage
    photo = ImageTk.PhotoImage(image=image)
    # Update the label with the new image
    self.label.config(image=photo)
    self.label.image = photo  # Keep a reference to avoid garbage collection
    self.root.update_idletasks()  # Update the GUI
```

This change will ensure that the video feed is displayed within the Tkinter window, maintaining a consistent GUI experience.

Task: "Please help me implement a Python program to create a real-time Object Detection and Tracking system for an ISR drone on an NVIDIA Jetson Orin NX, utilizing YOLOv8 for detection and DeepSORT or ByteTrack for tracking, integrating with live camera feeds, outputting real-time metadata, and optimizing for efficiency with TensorRT.".

"main.py
```python
'''
Main application file for real-time object detection and tracking.
'''
import cv2
from gui import App
from detection import YOLOv8Detector
from tracking import Tracker
from utils import optimize_with_tensorrt
def initialize_camera():
    # Initialize camera feed
    cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)  # Assuming the first camera device
    return cap
def initialize_yolo():
    # Load YOLOv8 model
    detector = YOLOv8Detector()
    return detector
def initialize_tracker():
    # Initialize tracker
    tracker = Tracker()
    return tracker
def process_frame(frame, detector, tracker):
    # Detect objects
    detections = detector.detect_objects(frame)
    # Update tracker
    tracks = tracker.update_tracks(detections)
    return tracks
def main():
    # Initialize components
    cap = initialize_camera()
    detector = initialize_yolo()
    tracker = initialize_tracker()
    # Optimize models with TensorRT
    optimize_with_tensorrt(detector)
    # Initialize GUI
    app = App()
    while True:
        ret, frame = cap.read()
        if not ret:
            break
        # Process frame
        tracks = process_frame(frame, detector, tracker)
        # Update GUI
        app.display_frame(frame)
        app.display_metadata(tracks)
        # Break on 'q' key press
        if cv2.waitKey(1) & 0xFF == ord('q'):
            break
    cap.release()
    cv2.destroyAllWindows()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

gui.py
```python
'''
GUI module for displaying video feed and metadata.
'''
import cv2
from tkinter import Tk, Label
class App:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = Tk()
        self.setup_ui()
    def setup_ui(self):
        self.root.title("Object Detection and Tracking")
        self.label = Label(self.root)
        self.label.pack()
    def display_frame(self, frame):
        # Convert frame to a format suitable for Tkinter
        cv2.imshow("Frame", frame)
    def display_metadata(self, tracks):
        # Display metadata in the GUI
        print("Tracks:", tracks)
    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()
```

detection.py
```python
'''
Detection module using YOLOv8.
'''
import torch
from ultralytics import YOLO
import numpy as np
import pycuda.driver as cuda
class YOLOv8Detector:
    def __init__(self, model_path='yolov8.pt'):
        # Load YOLOv8 model
        self.model = YOLO(model_path)
        self.engine = None
        self.context = None
        self.d_input = None
        self.d_output = None
        self.input_shape = None
        self.output_shape = None
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        if self.engine is not None:
            # Preprocess the frame
            frame_resized = cv2.resize(frame, (self.input_shape[2], self.input_shape[1]))
            frame_normalized = frame_resized.astype(np.float32) / 255.0
            frame_transposed = np.transpose(frame_normalized, (2, 0, 1)).ravel()
            # Transfer input data to the GPU
            cuda.memcpy_htod(self.d_input, frame_transposed)
            # Run inference
            self.context.execute_v2(bindings=[int(self.d_input), int(self.d_output)])
            # Transfer predictions back from the GPU
            output = np.empty(self.output_shape, dtype=np.float32)
            cuda.memcpy_dtoh(output, self.d_output)
            # Process output
            detections = self.process_output(output)
        else:
            # Fallback to PyTorch model if TensorRT is not available
            results = self.model(frame)
            detections = []
            for result in results.xyxy[0]:  # Assuming results are in xyxy format
                x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = result
                detections.append({
                    'bbox': [x1.item(), y1.item(), x2.item(), y2.item()],
                    'confidence': conf.item(),
                    'class': int(cls.item())
                })
        return detections
    def process_output(self, output):
        # Process the output from TensorRT inference
        detections = []
        for det in output:
            x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = det
            detections.append({
                'bbox': [x1, y1, x2, y2],
                'confidence': conf,
                'class': int(cls)
            })
        return detections
```

tracking.py
```python
'''
Tracking module using DeepSORT.
'''
from deep_sort.deep_sort import DeepSort
import numpy as np
class Tracker:
    def __init__(self):
        # Initialize DeepSORT tracker
        self.tracker = DeepSort(
            model_path='deep_sort_model.ckpt',  # Path to the DeepSORT model
            max_dist=0.2,
            min_confidence=0.3,
            nms_max_overlap=0.5,
            max_iou_distance=0.7,
            max_age=70,
            n_init=3,
            nn_budget=100
        )
    def update_tracks(self, detections):
        # Convert detections to the format required by DeepSORT
        bbox_xywh = np.array([det['bbox'] for det in detections])
        confidences = np.array([det['confidence'] for det in detections])
        classes = np.array([det['class'] for det in detections])
        # Update tracker with new detections
        tracks = self.tracker.update(bbox_xywh, confidences, classes)
        # Format tracks for output
        formatted_tracks = []
        for track in tracks:
            formatted_tracks.append({
                'track_id': track.track_id,
                'bbox': track.to_tlbr(),
                'class': track.cls,
                'confidence': track.confidence
            })
        return formatted_tracks
```

utils.py
```python
'''
Utility functions for optimization and other tasks.
'''
import tensorrt as trt
import pycuda.driver as cuda
import pycuda.autoinit
def optimize_with_tensorrt(detector):
    '''
    Optimize the YOLOv8 model with TensorRT.
    '''
    # Create a TensorRT logger
    logger = trt.Logger(trt.Logger.WARNING)
    # Create a builder and network
    builder = trt.Builder(logger)
    network = builder.create_network(1 << int(trt.NetworkDefinitionCreationFlag.EXPLICIT_BATCH))
    # Parse the ONNX model to TensorRT
    onnx_path = 'yolov8.onnx'  # Assuming the model is converted to ONNX format
    with trt.OnnxParser(network, logger) as parser:
        with open(onnx_path, 'rb') as model:
            if not parser.parse(model.read()):
                print('ERROR: Failed to parse the ONNX file.')
                for error in range(parser.num_errors):
                    print(parser.get_error(error))
                return
    # Build the engine
    builder.max_workspace_size = 1 << 30  # 1GB
    builder.max_batch_size = 1
    engine = builder.build_cuda_engine(network)
    # Allocate buffers for input and output
    input_shape = network.get_input(0).shape
    output_shape = network.get_output(0).shape
    input_size = trt.volume(input_shape) * trt.float32.itemsize
    output_size = trt.volume(output_shape) * trt.float32.itemsize
    d_input = cuda.mem_alloc(input_size)
    d_output = cuda.mem_alloc(output_size)
    # Create a context
    context = engine.create_execution_context()
    # Store the optimized engine and context in the detector
    detector.engine = engine
    detector.context = context
    detector.d_input = d_input
    detector.d_output = d_output
    detector.input_shape = input_shape
    detector.output_shape = output_shape
```

Comments on Codes:
"The code provided is mostly well-structured and follows the requirements. However, there is a critical issue regarding the integration of the GUI with the main loop. The current implementation uses OpenCV's `cv2.imshow` for displaying frames, which conflicts with the Tkinter GUI event loop. This can cause the application to hang or not display the GUI properly. 

To fix this, you should integrate the video feed display into the Tkinter GUI instead of using `cv2.imshow`. Here's a suggestion on how to do it:

1. Convert the OpenCV frame to a format that Tkinter can display (e.g., using PIL or directly with Tkinter's PhotoImage).
2. Update the `display_frame` method in `gui.py` to use Tkinter widgets for displaying the video feed.

Here's an example modification for the `display_frame` method:

```python
from PIL import Image, ImageTk

def display_frame(self, frame):
    # Convert the frame to RGB format
    frame_rgb = cv2.cvtColor(frame, cv2.COLOR_BGR2RGB)
    # Convert the frame to a PIL Image
    image = Image.fromarray(frame_rgb)
    # Convert the PIL Image to a PhotoImage
    photo = ImageTk.PhotoImage(image=image)
    # Update the label with the new image
    self.label.config(image=photo)
    self.label.image = photo  # Keep a reference to avoid garbage collection
    self.root.update_idletasks()  # Update the GUI
```

This change will ensure that the video feed is displayed within the Tkinter window, maintaining a consistent GUI experience."

main.py
```python
'''
Main application file for real-time object detection and tracking.
'''
import cv2
from gui import App
from detection import YOLOv8Detector
from tracking import Tracker
from utils import optimize_with_tensorrt

def initialize_camera():
    # Initialize camera feed
    cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)  # Assuming the first camera device
    return cap

def initialize_yolo():
    # Load YOLOv8 model
    detector = YOLOv8Detector()
    return detector

def initialize_tracker():
    # Initialize tracker
    tracker = Tracker()
    return tracker

def process_frame(frame, detector, tracker):
    # Detect objects
    detections = detector.detect_objects(frame)
    # Update tracker
    tracks = tracker.update_tracks(detections)
    return tracks

def main():
    # Initialize components
    cap = initialize_camera()
    detector = initialize_yolo()
    tracker = initialize_tracker()
    # Optimize models with TensorRT
    optimize_with_tensorrt(detector)
    # Initialize GUI
    app = App()
    while True:
        ret, frame = cap.read()
        if not ret:
            break
        # Process frame
        tracks = process_frame(frame, detector, tracker)
        # Update GUI
        app.display_frame(frame)
        app.display_metadata(tracks)
        # Break on 'q' key press
        if cv2.waitKey(1) & 0xFF == ord('q'):
            break
    cap.release()
    cv2.destroyAllWindows()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

```python
import cv2

class App:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = Tk()
        self.setup_ui()

    def setup_ui(self):
        self.root.title("Object Detection and Tracking")
        self.label = Label(self.root)
        self.label.pack()

    def display_frame(self, frame):
        # Convert the frame to RGB format
        frame_rgb = cv2.cvtColor(frame, cv2.COLOR_BGR2RGB)
        # Convert the frame to a PIL Image
        image = Image.fromarray(frame_rgb)
        # Convert the PIL Image to a PhotoImage
        photo = ImageTk.PhotoImage(image=image)
        # Update the label with the new image
        self.label.config(image=photo)
        self.label.image = photo  # Keep a reference to avoid garbage collection
        self.root.update_idletasks()  # Update the GUI

    def display_metadata(self, tracks):
        # Display metadata in the GUI
        print("Tracks:", tracks)

    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()
```

detection.py
```python
'''
Detection module using YOLOv8.
'''
import torch
from ultralytics import YOLO
import numpy as np
import pycuda.driver as cuda

class YOLOv8Detector:
    def __init__(self, model_path='yolov8.pt'):
        # Load YOLOv8 model
        self.model = YOLO(model_path)
        self.engine = None
        self.context = None
        self.d_input = None
        self.d_output = None
        self.input_shape = None
        self.output_shape = None

    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        if self.engine is not None:
            # Preprocess the frame
            frame_resized = cv2.resize(frame, (self.input_shape[2], self.input_shape[1]))
            frame_normalized = frame_resized.astype(np.float32) / 255.0
            frame_transposed = np.transpose(frame_normalized, (2, 0, 1)).ravel()
            # Transfer input data to the GPU
            cuda.memcpy_htod(self.d_input, frame_transposed)
            # Run inference
            self.context.execute_v2(bindings=[int(self.d_input), int(self.d_output)])
            # Transfer predictions back from the GPU
            output = np.empty(self.output_shape, dtype=np.float32)
            cuda.memcpy_dtoh(output, self.d_output)
            # Process output
            detections = self.process_output(output)
        else:
            # Fallback to PyTorch model if TensorRT is not available
            results = self.model(frame)
            detections = []
            for result in results.xyxy[0]:  # Assuming results are in xyxy format
                x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = result
                detections.append({
                    'bbox': [x1.item(), y1.item(), x2.item(), y2.item()],
                    'confidence': conf.item(),
                    'class': int(cls.item())
                })
        return detections

    def process_output(self, output):
        # Process the output from TensorRT inference
        detections = []
        for det in output:
            x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = det
            detections.append({
                'bbox': [x1, y1, x2, y2],
                'confidence': conf,
                'class': int(cls)
            })
        return detections
```

tracking.py
```python
'''
Tracking module using DeepSORT.
'''
from deep_sort.deep_sort import DeepSort
import numpy as np

class Tracker:
    def __init__(self):
        # Initialize DeepSORT tracker
        self.tracker = DeepSort(
            model_path='deep_sort_model.ckpt',  # Path to the DeepSORT model
            max_dist=0.2,
            min_confidence=0.3,
            nms_max_overlap=0.5,
            max_iou_distance=0.7,
            max_age=70,
            n_init=3,
            nn_budget=100
        )

    def update_tracks(self, detections):
        # Convert detections to the format required by DeepSORT
        bbox_xywh = np.array([det['bbox'] for det in detections])
        confidences = np.array([det['confidence'] for det in detections])
        classes = np.array([det['class'] for det in detections])
        # Update tracker with new detections
        tracks = self.tracker.update(bbox_xywh, confidences, classes)
        # Format tracks for output
        formatted_tracks = []
        for track in tracks:
            formatted_tracks.append({
                'track_id': track.track_id,
                'bbox': track.to_tlbr(),
                'class': track.cls,
                'confidence': track.confidence
            })
        return formatted_tracks
```

'''
Utility functions for optimization and other tasks.
'''
import tensorrt as trt
import pycuda.driver as cuda
import pycuda.autoinit

def optimize_with_tensorrt(detector):
    '''
    Optimize the YOLOv8 model with TensorRT.
    '''
    # Create a TensorRT logger
    logger = trt.Logger(trt.Logger.WARNING)
    # Create a builder and network
    builder = trt.Builder(logger)
    network = builder.create_network(1 << int(trt.NetworkDefinitionCreationFlag.EXPLICIT_BATCH))
    # Parse the ONNX

gui.py
```python
'''
GUI module for displaying video feed and metadata.
'''
import cv2
from tkinter import Tk, Label
from PIL import Image, ImageTk

class App:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = Tk()
        self.setup_ui()

    def setup_ui(self):
        self.root.title("Object Detection and Tracking")
        self.label = Label(self.root)
        self.label.pack()

    def display_frame(self, frame):
        # Convert the frame to RGB format
        frame_rgb = cv2.cvtColor(frame, cv2.COLOR_BGR2RGB)
        # Convert the frame to a PIL Image
        image = Image.fromarray(frame_rgb)
        # Convert the PIL Image to a PhotoImage
        photo = ImageTk.PhotoImage(image=image)
        # Update the label with the new image
        self.label.config(image=photo)
        self.label.image = photo  # Keep a reference to avoid garbage collection
        self.root.update_idletasks()  # Update the GUI

    def display_metadata(self, tracks):
        # Display metadata in the GUI
        print("Tracks:", tracks)

    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()
```

detection.py
```python
'''
Detection module using YOLOv8.
'''
import torch
from ultralytics import YOLO
import numpy as np
import pycuda.driver as cuda

class YOLOv8Detector:
    def __init__(self, model_path='yolov8.pt'):
        # Load YOLOv8 model
        self.model = YOLO(model_path)
        self.engine = None
        self.context = None
        self.d_input = None
        self.d_output = None
        self.input_shape = None
        self.output_shape = None

    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        if self.engine is not None:
            # Preprocess the frame
            frame_resized = cv2.resize(frame, (self.input_shape[2], self.input_shape[1]))
            frame_normalized = frame_resized.astype(np.float32) / 255.0
            frame_transposed = np.transpose(frame_normalized, (2, 0, 1)).ravel()
            # Transfer input data to the GPU
            cuda.memcpy_htod(self.d_input, frame_transposed)
            # Run inference
            self.context.execute_v2(bindings=[int(self.d_input), int(self.d_output)])
            # Transfer predictions back from the GPU
            output = np.empty(self.output_shape, dtype=np.float32)
            cuda.memcpy_dtoh(output, self.d_output)
            # Process output
            detections = self.process_output(output)
        else:
            # Fallback to PyTorch model if TensorRT is not available
            results = self.model(frame)
            detections = []
            for result in results.xyxy[0]:  # Assuming results are in xyxy format
                x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = result
                detections.append({
                    'bbox': [x1.item(), y1.item(), x2.item(), y2.item()],
                    'confidence': conf.item(),
                    'class': int(cls.item())
                })
        return detections

    def process_output(self, output):
        # Process the output from TensorRT inference
        detections = []
        for det in output:
            x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = det
            detections.append({
                'bbox': [x1, y1, x2, y2],
                'confidence': conf,
                'class': int(cls)
            })
        return detections
```

"main.py
```python
'''
Main application file for real-time object detection and tracking.
'''
import cv2
from gui import App
from detection import YOLOv8Detector
from tracking import Tracker
from utils import optimize_with_tensorrt
def initialize_camera():
    # Initialize camera feed
    cap = cv2.VideoCapture(0)  # Assuming the first camera device
    return cap
def initialize_yolo():
    # Load YOLOv8 model
    detector = YOLOv8Detector()
    return detector
def initialize_tracker():
    # Initialize tracker
    tracker = Tracker()
    return tracker
def process_frame(frame, detector, tracker):
    # Detect objects
    detections = detector.detect_objects(frame)
    # Update tracker
    tracks = tracker.update_tracks(detections)
    return tracks
def main():
    # Initialize components
    cap = initialize_camera()
    detector = initialize_yolo()
    tracker = initialize_tracker()
    # Optimize models with TensorRT
    optimize_with_tensorrt(detector)
    # Initialize GUI
    app = App()
    while True:
        ret, frame = cap.read()
        if not ret:
            break
        # Process frame
        tracks = process_frame(frame, detector, tracker)
        # Update GUI
        app.display_frame(frame)
        app.display_metadata(tracks)
        # Break on 'q' key press
        if cv2.waitKey(1) & 0xFF == ord('q'):
            break
    cap.release()
    cv2.destroyAllWindows()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

gui.py
```python
'''
GUI module for displaying video feed and metadata.
'''
import cv2
from tkinter import Tk, Label
from PIL import Image, ImageTk
class App:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = Tk()
        self.setup_ui()
    def setup_ui(self):
        self.root.title("Object Detection and Tracking")
        self.label = Label(self.root)
        self.label.pack()
    def display_frame(self, frame):
        # Convert the frame to RGB format
        frame_rgb = cv2.cvtColor(frame, cv2.COLOR_BGR2RGB)
        # Convert the frame to a PIL Image
        image = Image.fromarray(frame_rgb)
        # Convert the PIL Image to a PhotoImage
        photo = ImageTk.PhotoImage(image=image)
        # Update the label with the new image
        self.label.config(image=photo)
        self.label.image = photo  # Keep a reference to avoid garbage collection
        self.root.update_idletasks()  # Update the GUI
    def display_metadata(self, tracks):
        # Display metadata in the GUI
        print("Tracks:", tracks)
    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()
```

detection.py
```python
'''
Detection module using YOLOv8.
'''
import torch
from ultralytics import YOLO
import numpy as np
import pycuda.driver as cuda
class YOLOv8Detector:
    def __init__(self, model_path='yolov8.pt'):
        # Load YOLOv8 model
        self.model = YOLO(model_path)
        self.engine = None
        self.context = None
        self.d_input = None
        self.d_output = None
        self.input_shape = None
        self.output_shape = None
    def detect_objects(self, frame):
        if self.engine is not None:
            # Preprocess the frame
            frame_resized = cv2.resize(frame, (self.input_shape[2], self.input_shape[1]))
            frame_normalized = frame_resized.astype(np.float32) / 255.0
            frame_transposed = np.transpose(frame_normalized, (2, 0, 1)).ravel()
            # Transfer input data to the GPU
            cuda.memcpy_htod(self.d_input, frame_transposed)
            # Run inference
            self.context.execute_v2(bindings=[int(self.d_input), int(self.d_output)])
            # Transfer predictions back from the GPU
            output = np.empty(self.output_shape, dtype=np.float32)
            cuda.memcpy_dtoh(output, self.d_output)
            # Process output
            detections = self.process_output(output)
        else:
            # Fallback to PyTorch model if TensorRT is not available
            results = self.model(frame)
            detections = []
            for result in results.xyxy[0]:  # Assuming results are in xyxy format
                x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = result
                detections.append({
                    'bbox': [x1.item(), y1.item(), x2.item(), y2.item()],
                    'confidence': conf.item(),
                    'class': int(cls.item())
                })
        return detections
    def process_output(self, output):
        # Process the output from TensorRT inference
        detections = []
        for det in output:
            x1, y1, x2, y2, conf, cls = det
            detections.append({
                'bbox': [x1, y1, x2, y2],
                'confidence': conf,
                'class': int(cls)
            })
        return detections
```

tracking.py
```python
'''
Tracking module using DeepSORT.
'''
from deep_sort.deep_sort import DeepSort
import numpy as np
class Tracker:
    def __init__(self):
        # Initialize DeepSORT tracker
        self.tracker = DeepSort(
            model_path='deep_sort_model.ckpt',  # Path to the DeepSORT model
            max_dist=0.2,
            min_confidence=0.3,
            nms_max_overlap=0.5,
            max_iou_distance=0.7,
            max_age=70,
            n_init=3,
            nn_budget=100
        )
    def update_tracks(self, detections):
        # Convert detections to the format required by DeepSORT
        bbox_xywh = np.array([det['bbox'] for det in detections])
        confidences = np.array([det['confidence'] for det in detections])
        classes = np.array([det['class'] for det in detections])
        # Update tracker with new detections
        tracks = self.tracker.update(bbox_xywh, confidences, classes)
        # Format tracks for output
        formatted_tracks = []
        for track in tracks:
            formatted_tracks.append({
                'track_id': track.track_id,
                'bbox': track.to_tlbr(),
                'class': track.cls,
                'confidence': track.confidence
            })
        return formatted_tracks
```

utils.py
```python
'''
Utility functions for optimization and other tasks.
'''
import tensorrt as trt
import pycuda.driver as cuda
import pycuda.autoinit
def optimize_with_tensorrt(detector):
    '''
    Optimize the YOLOv8 model with TensorRT.
    '''
    # Create a TensorRT logger
    logger = trt.Logger(trt.Logger.WARNING)
    # Create a builder and network
    builder = trt.Builder(logger)
    network = builder.create_network(1 << int(trt.NetworkDefinitionCreationFlag.EXPLICIT_BATCH))
    # Parse the ONNX model to TensorRT
    onnx_path = 'yolov8.onnx'  # Assuming the model is converted to ONNX format
    with trt.OnnxParser(network, logger) as parser:
        with open(onnx_path, 'rb') as model:
            if not parser.parse(model.read()):
                print('ERROR: Failed to parse the ONNX file.')
                for error in range(parser.num_errors):
                    print(parser.get_error(error))
                return
    # Build the engine
    builder.max_workspace_size = 1 << 30  # 1GB
    builder.max_batch_size = 1
    engine = builder.build_cuda_engine(network)
    # Allocate buffers for input and output
    input_shape = network.get_input(0).shape
    output_shape = network.get_output(0).shape
    input_size = trt.volume(input_shape) * trt.float32.itemsize
    output_size = trt.volume(output_shape) * trt.float32.itemsize
    d_input = cuda.mem_alloc(input_size)
    d_output = cuda.mem_alloc(output_size)
    # Create a context
    context = engine.create_execution_context()
    # Store the optimized engine and context in the detector
    detector.engine = engine
    detector.context = context
    detector.d_input = d_input
    detector.d_output = d_output
    detector.input_shape = input_shape
    detector.output_shape = output_shape
```

Additionally, the TensorRT optimization process is not guaranteed to be compatible with all YOLOv8 models directly without proper conversion and testing. This could lead to runtime errors if the ONNX model is not correctly prepared or if the TensorRT optimization fails.

### Suggested Fix:

1. **Ensure ONNX Conversion**: Before optimizing with TensorRT, ensure that the YOLOv8 model is converted to ONNX format. This can be done using a conversion script or tool that supports YOLOv8 to ONNX conversion.

2. **Error Handling for TensorRT Optimization**: Add error handling in the `optimize_with_tensorrt` function to manage cases where the ONNX model cannot be parsed or the TensorRT engine cannot be built.

3. **Validation of TensorRT Optimization**: After optimization, validate the TensorRT engine by running a test inference to ensure that it produces expected results.

4. **Documentation**: Add comments and documentation to guide users on how to convert the YOLOv8 model to ONNX format and any prerequisites needed for TensorRT optimization.

**[Seminar Conclusion]**:

 The code provided is mostly well-structured and aligns with the task requirements. However, there is a critical issue regarding the integration of the TensorRT optimization process and the handling of the YOLOv8 model. The `optimize_with_tensorrt` function assumes that the YOLOv8 model is already converted to an ONNX format, which is not shown in the code. Additionally, the TensorRT optimization process is not guaranteed to be compatible with all YOLOv8 models directly without proper conversion and testing. This could lead to runtime errors if the ONNX model is not correctly prepared or if the TensorRT optimization fails.

### Suggested Fix:

1. **Ensure ONNX Conversion**: Before optimizing with TensorRT, ensure that the YOLOv8 model is converted to ONNX format. This can be done using a conversion script or tool that supports YOLOv8 to ONNX conversion.

2. **Error Handling for TensorRT Optimization**: Add error handling in the `optimize_with_tensorrt` function to manage cases where the ONNX model cannot be parsed or the TensorRT engine cannot be built.

3. **Validation of TensorRT Optimization**: After optimization, validate the TensorRT engine by running a test inference to ensure that it produces expected results.

4. **Documentation**: Add comments and documentation to guide users on how to convert the YOLOv8 model to ONNX format and any prerequisites needed for TensorRT optimization.

By addressing these points, the code will be more robust and user-friendly, ensuring that the object detection and tracking system operates efficiently on the NVIDIA Jetson Orin NX.

Initialize DeepSORT tracker\n        self.tracker = DeepSort(\n            model_path=\'deep_sort_model.ckpt\',  # Path to the DeepSORT model\n            max_dist=0.2,\n            min_confidence=0.3,\n            nms_max_overlap=0.5,\n            max_iou_distance=0.7,\n            max_age=70,\n            n_init=3,\n            nn_budget=100\n        )\n\n    def update_tracks(self, detections):\n        # Create a TensorRT logger\n    logger = trt.Logger(trt.Logger.WARNING)\n    # Create a builder and network\n    builder = trt.Builder(logger)\n    network = builder.create_network(1 &lt;&lt; int(trt.NetworkDefinitionCreationFlag.EXPLICIT_BATCH))\n    # Build the engine\n    builder.max_workspace_size = 1 &lt;&lt; 30  # 1GB\n    builder.max_batch_size = 1\n    engine = builder.build_cuda_engine(network)\n    # Allocate buffers for input and output\n    input_shape = network.get_input(0).shape\n    output_shape = network.get_output(0).shape\n    input_size = trt.volume(input_shape) * trt.float32.itemsize\n    output_size = trt.volume(output_shape) * trt.float32.itemsize\n    d_input = cuda.mem_alloc(input_size)\n    d_output = cuda.mem_alloc(output_size)\n    # Create a context\n    context = engine.create_execution_context()\n    # Store the optimized engine and context in the detector\n    detector.engine = engine\n    detector.context = context\n    detector.d_input = d_input\n    detector.d_output = d_output\n    detector.input_shape = input_shape\n    detector.output_shape = output_shape\n``\n\n', 'images': '', 'comments': 'The code provided is mostly well-structured and aligns with the task requirements. Task: "Please help me implement a Python program to create a real-time Object Detection and Tracking system for an ISR drone on an NVIDIA Jetson Orin NX, utilizing YOLOv8 for detection and DeepSORT or ByteTrack for tracking, integrating with live camera feeds, outputting real-time metadata, and optimizing for efficiency with TensorRT.".

Programming Language: " Python"
